Dear Mr. Kunioka: 
As requested, Geolabs, Inc. provided geotechnical engineering observation and 
consultation services during the micropile foundation installation work for the above project. 
This letter report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observations during the 
installation of micropile foundations for the new Scalping Plant structures in Kahului on the 
Island of Maui, Hawaii. The project location and general vicinity are shown on the Project 
Location Map, Plate 1. 
In general, this letter report presents our field observations and the results of load 
testing performed for the production micropiles, and our findings and recommendations for 
the micropile foundation for the project.  
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The Scalping Plant is located within the existing Kahului airport pump station in 
Kahului on the island of Maui, Hawaii. The new concrete equipment pads will be supported 
by 7.0-inch diameter micropiles with a design load capacity of 64 kips. A layout of the 
proposed foundations is presented on the Micropile Location Plan, Plate 2. Due to the 
Akinaka & Associates, Ltd.  
Page 2 
W.O. 7721-20B (Micropile Foundation Installation Observation Report) 
April 1, 2021 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
relatively high structural loads, soft ground conditions near the existing ground surface, 
and potential liquefaction in the event of an earthquake, we recommended that the new 
equipment pads be supported on a deep foundation system consisting of micropiles. 
MICROPILE INSTALLATION AND TESTING 
Geotechnical recommendations for the micropile foundations were presented in our 
referenced letter report dated March 18, 2020, and our subsequent addendum dated 
May 22, 2020. The purpose of our geotechnical engineering observation and consultation 
services was to observe the micropile foundation installation and testing for general 
conformance with our recommendations. 
Based on the anticipated subsurface conditions at the site, the micropiles were 
specified to extend through very soft to soft alluvium and very loose to loose coralline 
detritus, and develop load capacity in the underlying competent stiff alluvium and basalt rock 
formation.  
Kelikai, Inc. installed a total of 48 production micropiles from January 4, 2021 through 
February 23, 2021 at the approximate locations shown on the Micropile Location Plan, 
Plate 2. The micropile locations were provided by Kelikai, Inc. Details of the micropile 
installation are presented in the micropile installation records in Appendix A. 
In general, the micropiles were installed using a TEI DR-TD 75 drill rig equipped with 
a down-the-hole hammer and advanced with 7.0-inch OD (Outside Diameter) steel casing 
to the specified depth of the micropile to create a drilled hole of at least 7.0 inches in 
diameter.  
After the drilled holes were extended to the specified depth and cleaned out, the 
micropiles were initially grouted. Grout was batched on-site utilizing a colloidal high-shear 
and high-speed ChemGrout CG-620 mixer equipped with a grout pump. The grout mix 
consisted of one sack of 94-pound Portland Cement Type I and/or II, 87 pounds of masonry 
sand, and 5 gallons of water.  
The grout was pumped into the cased hole through a PVC tremie pipe starting from 
the bottom of the cased hole. After clean grout appeared at the top of the cased hole, a 
reinforcing bar with centralizers was placed in the cased hole. 
The temporary steel casing was removed one section at a time and re-grouted as 
necessary to maintain the grout level near the top of the casing. This process continued until 
the bottom of the steel casing reached the top of the bond zone. The permanent casing was 
then plunged to a final depth of approximately 4 feet into the bearing layer.  
It should be noted that Micropile Nos. R-3, R-7, and R-11 were relocated and installed 
6 inches to the west due to an existing 8-inch waterline. 
Akinaka & Associates, Ltd.  
Page 3 
W.O. 7721-20B (Micropile Foundation Installation Observation Report) 
April 1, 2021 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
During drilling work, an annulus formed between the existing ground surface and the 
upper micropile casing at 19 micropile locations. To ensure adequate lateral resistance, the 
voids were filled with a 3,000 psi grout mix on February 26, 2021. The micropiles with 
grouted annuli are noted on the Micropile Installation Summary, Plates A-1.1 and A-1.2. 
Micropile Proof Load Testing 
In order to evaluate the load carrying capacities of the installed micropiles, five proof 
tests were conducted on five production micropiles. The proof tests were conducted on 
Micropile Nos. R-2, N-13, N-7, E-12, and N-24 on March 3 and 4, 2021. All five micropiles 
were loaded to a maximum test load of 85.1 kips (133 percent of the design load). The 
maximum test load of about 85.1 kips was held for 10 minutes to evaluate creep effects. 
Subsequently, Micropile Nos. R-2 and N-13 were unloaded to zero load in one load 
decrement, while Micropile Nos. N-7, E-12, and N-24 were unloaded to zero load in about 
five equal load decrements.  
In general, the proof-tested production micropiles met the acceptance criteria 
specified in the project requirements. A summary of test results at the maximum test load 
(MTL) is provided in the following table. The results of the proof tests are presented in 
Appendix B.

FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS 
Based on our field observations of the micropile installation and micropile proof load 
tests performed by the subcontractor, it is our professional opinion that the production 
micropiles for the project have been installed to provide the design load capacity of 64 kips 
with tolerable movements. 
LIMITATIONS 
The results submitted herein are based, in part, upon our field observations and the 
micropile proof load tests performed during the micropile foundation installation work. It
